More Than Two Hundred Soldiers Killed and Injured

Reuters, Ouled Yellal, North Africa, 14th – Today, a French troop train carrying 510 soldiers derailed at high speed about 70 miles from here and fell into a valley. Fifty people were killed and eighty seriously injured. The cause of the accident is thought to be the collapse of the roadbed.

Guomin News Agency, Paris, 15th – A recent report from Ouled Yellal states that at least 120 officers and soldiers were killed and 150 injured in the African troop train derailment.

Dutch Sailors Cancel Strike

Reuters, Rotterdam, 15th – The Dutch shipping strike has been quite tense in the past half month. The sailors of the Rotterdam, belonging to the Holland America Line, even mutinied, causing the government to dispatch a warship to escort it into port. Today, representatives of both the shipowners and sailors gathered for a meeting and agreed that wages will not be reduced for the time being, for a period of one to six months. During this period, both parties will contact the government in order to resolve the entire issue. Therefore, from today, the sailors have canceled the general strike.

Promotion of Trade Takes on a New Look

German Industrial Circles are Preparing a World Tour Exhibition

Guomin News Agency, Berlin, 14th – German industrial circles are now discussing equipping a ship, to be named the German Exhibition Ship, to tour the world early next year. The voyage will last 18 months and pass through 70 foreign ports. The ship will carry purely German products for exhibition in each port, in order to promote Germany's export trade. German commercial firms wishing to take advantage of this opportunity will be charged very little. However, only commercial firms manufacturing first-class goods will be allowed to participate.

Important News

Northern Manchuria 8

Recent Situation of Active Volunteer Armies

Jilin, Dunhua, and Changchun are All Shaken

Japanese Army is Gradually Finding it Difficult to Cope

Harbin Correspondence: Recently, the floodwaters in Jilin and Heilongjiang have gradually receded, and transportation in various places has been restored somewhat. The volunteer armies, which have been dormant for many days, have resumed their activities in different directions. The most vigorous advances and the fiercest battles have been those of Li Haiqing's attack on Anda Station, Yang Yaojun's attack on Weishahe, Cai Hongyou's attack on Mulan, Xu Zihe's attack on Keshan, Tian Zhaoying's attack on Qingcheng, Li Tiande's attack on Bayan, Wang Delin's attack on Dunhua, Qiu Zhenhua's attack on Yushu, Wang Fuchen's attack on Dehui, Gong Changhai's attack on Jilin, and Ding Chao's attack on Fujin. The following is a summary of the key events:

Li Haiqing's Attack on Anda Two months ago, the Japanese side spread rumors, vaguely stating that Li Haiqing and Ma Zhanshan had died in battle in Angu Town, northwest of Hailun. At the time, all parties knew that this was false. It was not until August 27th, when news came that Anda Station was under pressure, that it was known that the person leading the troops to recapture it was Li Haiqing himself. Two days earlier, Li's advance team of about 2,000 had advanced to Anda County, surrounded the county seat, and launched a fierce attack. A regiment of puppet army cavalry was stationed in the city, defending it in cooperation with the puppet militia and police. The two sides engaged in a fierce battle. After attacking and defending for nearly four hours, the city was finally captured by Li's army. Most of the puppet army broke through and fled to Wangkui, while some were disarmed. On the 27th, Li Haiqing himself arrived with his troops and advanced towards Anda Station. First, he sent people with name cards of Ma Zhanshan and Li himself to the local military and police authorities and the leaders of the Chamber of Commerce, informing them that he would lead his troops into the city and that there should be no resistance. The puppet Heilongjiang army stationed at Anda Station consisted of about 400 cavalry and 800 infantry, with attached machine gun and mortar special companies. The station was garrisoned by a large squadron of the puppet special district guard, about 400 men. They planned to unite and resist. Before the plan could be finalized, Li's advance team had arrived, infiltrated the city streets, and surrounded and disarmed the puppet army before they could escape. The weapons of the puppet guard were also confiscated at the same time. By 2 p.m., Li's troops had entered the city in succession, numbering over 4,000. The chairman of the Chamber of Commerce was summoned and told to operate peacefully without fear. At the same time, he was ordered to hang the blue and white flag and issue a public notice to reassure the people. As a result, the merchants continued to operate as usual. At 6 p.m., Li dispatched 700 cavalry to Song Station, cut the telegraph wires, and demolished the tracks between Sartu and Song Station. The workers of the East Railway between the two stations were protected by Li's army and boarded a train at Sartu, ordering them to return to Harbin and report that Li Haiqing's Heilongjiang volunteer army had recaptured Anda. That evening, traffic on the Harbin-Manchuria railway was cut off, and telephone and telegram communications were disrupted. On the 29th, the Tadayama branch of the Amano Brigade of the Japanese army stationed in Heilongjiang, in conjunction with Japanese cavalry from Angangxi, went to attack on a train. At noon, the two sides made contact north of the railway, with intense artillery fire. At 1 p.m., three Japanese aircraft flew from Harbin to drop bombs, with the most bombs falling on the third and fourth streets in the city, destroying many shops and causing a large fire. At that time, Li Haiqing personally led his troops at the front line to supervise the battle. Wang Futing, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, braved the rain of bullets to go to the front and plead with Li to temporarily withdraw his troops to avoid excessive losses to the merchants. Li, unable to refuse the earnest request, led his troops to retreat to the Da Jingzi area, 40 miles outside the city, at 3 p.m. The Japanese army, seeing their momentum, did not dare to pursue. At about 4 p.m., a trainload of Japanese soldiers with over a thousand soldiers arrived from Harbin. The two teams joined forces and attempted to disembark to pursue the fleeing troops. At this time, Li's cavalry divided into two branches and outflanked Anda on the left and right, demolishing all the tracks and taking a surrounding posture, controlling the area from a distance. The Japanese army did not dare to leave the armored train and took a defensive posture inside and outside the station. Since the 30th, Li's troops have launched night attacks with cavalry. The Japanese army relied on armored vehicles to resist. Because there were no reinforcements, they were trapped. On September 3rd, Li's army advanced towards Qiqihar in large numbers, intending to strike directly at the provincial capital. Therefore, the situation in that direction became tense. Traffic on the Harbin-Manchuria railway has been cut off since August 27th and has not yet been restored. There will be major changes in the Angangxi and Boketu areas recently.

Yang Yaojun's Attack on Weishahe Yang Yaojun is the right-wing special operations unit of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, and he is in contact with Yang Zibin's brigade, operating near Acheng and Yimianpo. On August 24th, he once captured Acheng, but retreated because the Japanese army assisted the puppet Jilin army in defending it very strictly. On September 1st, Yang led more than 2,000 troops, along with about 600 members of the Big Sword Society and Red Spear Society, to the vicinity of Weishahe County. The Japanese army stationed in Yimianpo, upon hearing the news, immediately dispatched over a thousand cavalry and artillery, riding in armored trains, to resist the enemy. En route, their progress was impeded by the demolition of the tracks by Yang's troops. At the same time, the Big Sword Society and Red Spear Society surrounded and launched a fierce attack, trapping the Japanese army in a dilemma of advance and retreat. While the Big Sword Society was surrounding the Japanese army, Yang's main force took advantage of the gap and directly entered Weishahe County. The two battalions of puppet troops originally stationed there collapsed at the sight of them. Those who could not escape in time were disarmed. After entering the city, Yang's troops ordered the merchants to operate as usual. Except for requisitioning food for military use, the rest was left untouched. On the 2nd, the Japanese side dispatched a large number of troops from Harbin, protected by two aircraft, to repair the tracks and quickly drove to Weishahe, linking up with the Japanese army in Yimianpo to launch a fierce attack on Weishahe. They also used two heavy artillery pieces to bombard the city continuously, destroying many houses in the county seat. At the same time, aircraft flew back and forth dropping bombs. Yang's troops were threatened from above and retreated completely towards the Wujimi River at noon. On the 4th, they recaptured the Wujimi River. The details are still unknown.

Wang Delin's Attack on Dunhua Wang Delin and Gong Changhai's troops have formed a connection. Wang's troops deployed from Dongning and Ning'an, taking Dunhua and Jiaohe, to cut off the connection between the Japanese troops on the Jilin-Huiyuan Road and to destroy the construction of that road, coordinating with Gong Changhai's army to capture Jilin. Wang Jin, a foreign technician, set up an arsenal between Ning'an and Tokyo City to manufacture medicines, bullets, guns, and mortars. Therefore, the military supplies have been very plentiful recently. On the 2nd of this month, Wang personally led 4,000 troops to capture Dunhua. A Japanese regiment there was suddenly surrounded in the middle of the night, and they fled in disarray. After a chaotic battle lasting two hours, a captain, a sergeant major, and six sergeants were killed. Countless soldiers were killed and wounded. They left behind two mountain guns and an armored train. The remnants retreated to Huangni River. Wang's troops entered the city on the morning of the 3rd. Currently, Wang's troops in the Dongning area are still being transported to Dunhua, and they will concentrate their forces to advance towards Jilin. The Japanese army stationed in Jilin is unable to provide assistance to Dunhua due to the constraint of Gong Changhai's army. Therefore, since Dunhua was recovered by Wang's army, the market has been operating as usual. In addition, Wang's army attacked Dunhua about a dozen times before, but retreated due to lack of ammunition, with efforts failing at the last moment. It is understood that this place is the shield of Jidong and one of the important points of the Jilin-Huiyuan Road. Now that it has been recaptured, it is as if Jilin has lost an arm.

Gong Changhai's Attack on Jilin Gong Changhai's army is divided into two branches. One branch attacked the Ninth Road of the Jilin-Changchun Line, cutting off the connection between Jilin and Changchun. The other branch attacked Jilin, reaching Longtan Mountain and Wula, east of the city

Over 800 men came from the Jilin-Huiyuan Road to join forces, intending to capture the front of Jilin. The Japanese Second Division has gathered a large force inside the city, erected power grids on the four outskirts, and dug trenches to defend firmly. Although firing has not yet begun, the situation is very tense.

Qiu Zhenhua's Attack on Yushu The newly compiled special operations unit of the volunteer army Xing Zhanqing, Qiu Zhenhua's unit of about 800 men, advanced from Yanshou in mid-August to Yushu. On August 27th, they reached Xiangyang Pao in the Second District of Yushu. First, a small number of infantry used the green gauze screens as cover to advance to Gaojia Bridge, east of the county seat, 20 miles from Yushu County. They also ordered plainclothes troops to sneak into the city and cut the telegraph wires. In the afternoon, Qiu's army was already outside the city. The puppet army Liu Baolin only heard the news and hastily went out to fight. The soldiers had no fighting spirit and collapsed for the most part after a short engagement. The remnants led by Liu retreated to Xinli Village and telegraphed the Japanese army in Changchun and Harbin for assistance. Qiu's army entered the city in the afternoon, ordering the merchants and people to hang the blue and white flag to celebrate. On September 3rd, the Japanese army dispatched a large team of nearly 2,000 men, along with the puppet Jilin-Changchun Railway garrison, to attack. Two aircraft provided cover and dropped bombs. Qiu's army fought to the death, but eventually retreated towards Shulan due to being outnumbered. They will cross the Yitong River to coordinate with Feng Zhanhai's army in attacking Changchun.

Wang Fuchen's Attack on Dehui Wang Fuchen's unit of Feng Zhanhai's newly compiled infantry brigade entered Dehui at 6 a.m. on September 5th. The force numbered about 2,000, and their military appearance was very impressive. The Japanese side dispatched troops stationed in Yushu and the puppet garrison of Jin Bidong to provide assistance, but they have not yet made contact.

Ding Chao's Attack on Fujin The Yilan and Fujin areas were very strained yesterday. It is reported that Ding Chao has led his troops to attack Fujin. The Japanese side is resisting with a detachment, and the battle is quite fierce. Ding's army has abundant military supplies. The Japanese side claims that their heavy artillery's range and power are equal to that of the Japanese army. Therefore, the Japanese army is already at a disadvantage. In addition, Xu Jingde's Heilongjiang army is advancing from Luobei towards Suidong, intending to advance towards Hegang to reclaim the coal mines. Volunteer armies are蜂拥[fēng yōng] - swarming/thronging - active in all directions, and it is not easy for the Japanese army to cope with them. (September 7th)

Cai Hongyou's Attack on Mulan Cai Hongyou's brigade of the Heilongjiang army, on September 1st, linked up with Li Tiande's brigade and advanced in a roundabout way from the Hebei area, crossing the Tangyuan and Tonghe rivers, and attacking Bayan and Mulan separately. Cai Hongyou's brigade, numbering about 3,000, arrived in Mulan on the 2nd and surrounded the county seat to attack. The local militia rose up in response and disarmed a regiment of puppet troops stationed there. The Japanese 14th Division's infantry battalion was stationed at the pier. At first, they made contact with Cai's brigade, but when they saw the militia's defection, they fled in panic towards Tangyuan. Cai's brigade then entered the city peacefully, digging trenches and building defensive works on the four outskirts and along the riverbank. The local militia, upon receiving Cai's brigade's report that Ma Zhanshan would lead over 3,000 cavalry from Moergen to take Tongbei, and advance to Hailun and Suihua from the side, cheered and voluntarily donated money and food. Therefore, the morale of the Heilongjiang army is very high. A Japanese infantry regiment stationed in Yilan, riding on four puppet river defense warships and six civilian boats, sailed upstream along the river and bombarded the city with heavy artillery from the banks of the Mulan River on the 3rd. Cai's brigade and the militia defended along the river, resisting with all their might. Since the fire started on the morning of the 5th, four Japanese aircraft have dropped bombs many times, but because Cai's brigade had built trenches and defended effectively, the bombs did not have a significant effect after landing. As of today, the 3rd, they are still in the midst of attack and defense. The Japanese side has already dispatched two more battalions from Huachuan to provide assistance and they are currently en route.

Li Tiande's Attack on Bayan Li Tiande's army entered Bayan on September 3rd. The Japanese army headquarters there, stationed with a company of guards, was surrounded and more than 70 men were killed. The remnants escaped back to Hulan on the Guangxin Wheel. The Japanese army has dispatched troops from the Hulan River to provide assistance, but they have not yet made contact as of yesterday. River traffic downstream has been cut off for several days.

Xu Zihe Captures Keshan Xu Zihe and Xu Baozhen divided the Heilongjiang army into two units at the end of August, each with about 4,000 men. Xu Baozhen advanced towards Nenjiang and Nehe to contain the Japanese army in that area, while Xu Zihe went south along the railway line to coordinate with Ma Zhanshan's main force between Tongbei and Moergen. Because the Japanese army on the Qike Road was densely deployed, there were not many clashes along the way, and they all detoured around in large circles. On September 2nd, they advanced to Keshan. Because the puppet Heilongjiang army, under Pu Datong, was stationed there with a thousand men, originally the mainstay of the Heilongjiang army's resistance against Japan after the war, Xu wanted to cooperate with this unit, so he launched a siege on the city. At the same time, he sent people secretly to persuade the leaders of the army. Most of the army agreed and responded by opening the north gate on the evening of the 2nd. Over 700 Japanese troops in the city were caught in a chaotic battle, with nearly half of them killed or wounded. The remnants broke through to Aolonggou. On the 3rd, most of the Japanese troops in Taianzhen rushed to provide assistance, with several aircraft dropping bombs in the air, injuring many people and horses. Xu's troops were unable to defend firmly and abandoned the city to retreat to Baiquan. The buildings in the city were destroyed by Japanese artillery fire, and the fire started very fiercely. It was not extinguished until the afternoon of the 5th, burning down about 20 stores and over 200 houses. ▲ Tian Zhaoying's Attack on Qingcheng Tian Zhaoying's army, numbering about 1,500, was also to coordinate with Ma Zhanshan's main force. On September 1st, they transferred from Suiling to Qingcheng. About 300 puppet troops in the city collapsed and fled at the news. The Heilongjiang army then entered the city and is now repairing the city walls and digging trenches, intending to make it a base for the Heilongjiang army's southward advance.

Zheng Jicheng Will Be Sent to Court for Trial 9

Military Law Department Has Prepared for Transfer

Jinan Correspondence: After Zhang Zongchang was assassinated, various circles in Shandong rose up to rescue Zheng Jicheng, sending letters and telegrams in droves, recounting Zhang Zongchang's various crimes and requesting the Central Government to grant Zheng a special pardon. Zhang Weicun, a standing committee member of the Provincial Party Department, also telegraphed various parties on the 6th, advocating a solution between law and human sentiment. The Provincial Party Department also telegraphed on the 9th, requesting the Central Government to grant Zheng a special pardon. Military Affairs Commission Chairman Chiang Kai-shek replied by telegram, advocating that Zheng be sent to court for trial, and if the sentence was too heavy, then the special pardon regulations could be invoked. The previous process has been detailed in the previous letter. Today, the Provincial Party Department received a reply telegram from the Central Executive Committee: "Telegram received. The case has been approved by the Standing Committee, and a letter has been sent to the Executive Yuan ordering the Ministry of Judicial Administration to transfer the case to the court for handling in accordance with the law. Central Executive Committee Secretariat, Printing Department." Standing committee member Zhang Weicun then took the telegram to the Provincial Government to meet with Chairman Han Fuqu and the other committee members, showed them the telegram, and prepared everything to await the arrival of the Ministry's dispatch before having Zheng Jicheng brought out by the Military Law Department, preparing a document to send him to court for trial in accordance with the law. It is also heard that the Provincial Government will cite three points in the telegram sending Zheng to court: (1) Zheng Jicheng assassinated Zhang to avenge his father's murder by Zhang, and the circumstances of calmly surrendering himself after killing Zhang at the station on the 3rd; (2) Zhang Zongchang's past deeds in Shandong, for which the Shandong Provincial Government had issued an arrest warrant; (3) Zhang Zongchang was inherently brutal, and Zheng Jinsheng had contributed to the revolution and had been killed, causing his family to be ruined. Judging by the time, the Provincial Government can send Zheng to court based on the Ministry's dispatch within the next week. After the judgment is made, it should then invoke the special pardon regulations to pardon Zheng. (September 14th)

National Palace Museum 10

National treasures are concentrated in the Palace Museum, passed down through generations for thousands of years. It is a symbol of China's five-thousand-year-old culture. Its historical origins are almost entirely contained within. It is not merely a collection of rare and exotic objects. During the monarchical era, the entire nation served one person, and these items were not easily seen by the people, nor were scholars able to study them. Since the relocation of the palace in 1924, the Palace Museum was established, opening exhibitions and circulating printed materials. This satisfies the yearning of antiquarians and provides material for scholarly research. Almost a decade has swiftly passed, its reputation resounding throughout the world, reaching foreign lands. Repeated translations draw visitors, almost every day. We have always taken pride in being an ancient country with a rich culture. It is only now that this cultural history is being revealed to the world. The treasures within are all related to cultural relics and inspire historical insights. We, the Chinese people, are fortunate to witness these rare treasures and should cherish them and use them to glorify the nation for future generations. However, since the establishment of the museum, there have been many disturbances. Recently, there have been rumors of relocation and even sale. A nation's foundation rests on both cultural virtue and military strength. We cannot emphasize military prowess, which is undeniable. If we cannot even safeguard this cultural area, and we commit an act that even autocratic rulers of the past would not have done, then it is truly lamentable. Therefore, I will briefly describe the establishment of the museum to show the difficulty of its creation, so that the people of the country will pay attention to it.

The richness of the museum's collection is difficult to fully describe, and its origin is hard to exhaust. The inspection reports already number in the dozens of volumes, and still are not enough to fully describe the collection. Regarding the establishment of the museum, in summary, it can be divided into several periods. First, I will describe the first period, which is Puyi's departure from the palace.

Puyi's departure from the palace was based on a decision made by the regency council on November 4, 1924. The executors were Lu Zhonglin, then the garrison commander, Zhang Bi, then the police commissioner, and Li Shizeng, as a representative of the people. During the execution, the National Army headquarters first disarmed the 1,200 guards stationed in the Qing Palace and Jingshan, then Lu and others sent representatives to meet Shao Ying and Zhu Yifan, requesting Puyi to leave the palace. After one meeting, Puyi agreed to leave, but stated that personal belongings inside the palace should be inspected, which could not be done in a day or two. Therefore, it was decided that Puyi would leave first, and at the same time, all eunuchs and maids in the palace were informed to pack up their belongings. At 4:10 PM, he left by car to his father's Prince Chun Mansion. At the same time, all affiliated institutions of the Qing court were automatically dissolved. Before leaving the palace, the national seal and the entire palace were returned to the Republic of China. The two old concubines in the palace were temporarily attended to by the palace eunuchs. As for the inspection of items, Shao Ying and three other members of the Qing court, as well as two representatives each from the Republic of China police department and the garrison department, were appointed as committee members. The State Council also appointed Li Shizeng as the chairman of the committee. At the same time, the sealing began, and the organizational regulations of the committee had already been approved by the cabinet. This was followed by the committee period.

During the relocation of the palace, the Beijing government had originally amended the preferential treatment conditions with Puyi, abolishing his honorary title, moving him out of the palace, and providing him with 500,000 yuan annually. However, after the Qing court left the palace, they continued to plot opposition. Therefore, these amended conditions were also implicitly abolished. The committee was formally established on November 20, with a total of fifteen members and three supervisors, and three more individuals were hired. In addition, each ministry sent two assistants. Of the fifteen committee members, five were from the Qing court, but none of them ever attended.

Not long after the regency cabinet was reorganized, Duan Qirui became the Chief Executive, which led to a slight change. He abruptly ordered the Ministry of Interior to instruct the committee to cease the inspection. The committee initially refused to comply, and the Ministry of Interior ultimately supported the committee's position. At that time, the committee was newly established and enthusiastically began its work, disregarding Duan's objections. Eventually, the State Council amended the measures, adding ministers and important officials to the existing committee as a buffer. By that time, Duan's willingness to acquiesce was due to the efforts of the committee members and the mediation of Supervisor Zhuang Yunkuan. Zhuang was known for his integrity and was respected by Duan, and his words resolved the matter. At the same time, the Ministry of Interior still strongly invited the five committee members from the Qing court, but they refused to come, as they intended to restore the monarchy and pursue other avenues, and were determined not to cooperate with the Republic of China. This was a helpless situation. Later, Puyi came to demand personal items, and the committee allowed it. However, the valuable furs and other items taken out of the Shenwu Gate were divided up by the Manchurian officials and eunuchs. Puyi received only a small portion. Subsequently, regarding the land deed of Qingfengsi, the Qing court accused the committee to Duan, while the committee presented evidence of restoration and requested the prosecutor's office to prosecute, in order to counteract the accusation. For a time, newspapers widely reported this. Eventually, the committee's receipt of the land deed was not addressed, and the restoration was not prosecuted by the prosecutor's office because it occurred before the general amnesty on January 1. Therefore, the compromise was likely the only solution.

The fifteen members of the committee were Wang Zhaoming (replaced by Yi Peiji), Cai Yuanpei (replaced by Jiang Menglin), Lu Zhonglin, Zhang Bi, Fan Yuanlian, Yu Tongkui, Chen Yuan, Shen Jianshi, Ge Wenjun, Shao Ying, Zai Run, Qiling, Bao Xi, and Luo Zhenyu, with Shao Ying and the following four as Qing court members. The supervisors were Wu Jingheng, Zhang Ji, and Zhuang Yunkuan, in addition to the police department, prosecutor's office, and education association.

The committee, recognizing that the Qing court was causing much obstruction and that only public disclosure could prevent it, decided to open the Palace Museum. It was formally established on Double Ten Day in 1925. First, the organizational outline was resolved. The inspection committee went to various palaces to extract exhibits, and the committee elected several directors of the museum, all well-known figures at the time. The opening on Double Ten Day was a great success, with tens of thousands of visitors. From inspection to public opening, the people were able to freely visit, and the Palace Museum became increasingly noticed by the people.

However, after a few months, the Palace Museum, due to political turmoil, transitioned from the period of directors' responsibility to the period of the maintenance committee. After the March 18 tragedy in 1926, Li Shizeng and Yi Peiji successively left Beijing. The museum was managed by a joint meeting of the board of directors, which elected Lu Yongxiang and Zhuang Yunkuan as maintainers. As Lu was not in Beijing, the responsibility fell solely on Zhuang. At that time, the troops were being transferred, and Zhuang consulted with the Ministry of Interior to borrow guards. The Ministry of Interior, seeking to intervene, gladly agreed to transfer its guards and the guards of the Ancient Artifacts Exhibition Hall under its management to the museum. However, the museum strongly opposed the Ministry of Interior's intervention and changed the positions of the officials sent by the ministry to advisors. The Ministry of Interior was displeased but could do nothing. At that time, due to insufficient funding, Zhuang even raised a private debt of 30,000 gold coins to meet the needs. However, on April 23, the Zhili-Shandong Allied Army suddenly sent troops to surround the Palace Museum, forcing it to be vacated. This was unexpected. Wang Shizhen, Zhao Erxun, and others immediately inquired with the Fengtian-Shandong generals, who all claimed to be unaware. Therefore, representatives were sent to negotiate, and the troops surrounding the palace were transferred elsewhere, fortunately resolving the crisis. However, a few months later, the cabinet changed again, with Du Xigui appointed and Wu Peifu effectively in charge. The Qing court, believing that Wu was easy to deal with, sent a letter to the State Council and Wu, seeking to restore preferential treatment. This caused a great uproar, and Wu rejected it. However, the State Council formally approved the reorganization of the museum, with the museum hiring twenty-one committee members and establishing six articles for safekeeping. The hired committee members elected Zhao Erxun as the chairman and Sun Baoqi as the vice-chairman. The museum staff insisted on three principles: no returning to Puyi, no selling, and no destruction. When the old and new were handed over, another handover committee was formed.

As the political situation changed, the affairs of the Palace Museum became the focus of public attention. Therefore, famous scholars established a maintenance association. After several meetings, Jiang Han was elected as the chairman, and Zhuang and Wang Chonghui as the vice-chairmen. Strict rules were established and filed with the Ministry of Interior. The Ministry of Interior also approved the establishment, approving temporary responsibility for maintenance. Once the formal organization was established, the association would be dissolved. Therefore, this temporary organization bore this great responsibility amidst the storms.

After the establishment of the maintenance association, it suffered from a lack of funding. Therefore, it was decided to dispose of expendable items, such as gold, silver, tea, and food that were not related to culture. Temporary bidding rules and temporary supervision rules were established, which seemed quite meticulous. When Zhang Zuolin became the Grand Marshal, the State Council decided that the Taimiao and Tangzi should be returned to the Ministry of Interior, and the military archives should be returned to the State Council. At the same time, there were those who advocated for investigation, as Zai Tao was serving as the aide-de-camp to the marshal and wanted to harm the museum. Fortunately, the authorities later realized the importance and, although they made slight changes to the organization, they still retained the committee and hired Wang Shizhen as the chairman, with Wang Shitoong and Yuan Jinkai as the vice-chairmen. This was followed by the period of Fengtian management. The committee hired by the State Council received the museum, and twenty-four secretaries were sent. The system was not changed. After seven months, the revolutionary army arrived in Beijing, and the National Government ordered Yi Peiji to take over. Funding was sought through the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity. The takeover was smooth, although there were some twists and turns with the Summer Palace and the Qing History Institute.

At that time, Jing Hengyi proposed selling and destroying the cultural relics. The museum staff was greatly shocked. Fortunately, Jing's proposal was quickly rejected. The National Government promulgated the organizational law of the Palace Museum and appointed directors, forming a board of directors. The board of directors then elected ten more members and appointed Li Shizeng as the chairman and Yi Peiji as the director, which has remained largely unchanged to this day.

Recently, the disposal of gold and silver has occurred. In fact, the disposal was regulated by the National Government last year, and everything must be done in accordance with the regulations, with the supervision of local judicial and academic circles. However, if the procedures are complete, it is not easy for corruption to occur. However, those who possess treasures are easily misled, and therefore, there are renewed rumors of selling treasures, some saying that the entire collection would be used to purchase military equipment, others saying that some negotiations have already taken place, others saying that relocation is a prelude to sale, and others saying that the main advocate of sale is expressing his anger. In fact, these treasures, which have existed for thousands of years, should not be discussed except for preservation. Moreover, the autocratic system of thousands of years was once overthrown, allowing the Palace to be transformed into a museum. The national essence is the soul of the country, and the people cannot be indifferent to the loss of cultural relics. The National Government had a ban on the export of old books last year. Considering this, wouldn't this be even more important and significant? It is hoped that the rumors are inaccurate.

Songjiang 11

Strange Robbery in Luzidiaowan In Luzidiaowan, a few people speaking with a foreign accent came to the Yidachang store on the 13th morning, pretending to buy sandalwood. Wu Shiyuan, a relative of the store owner Yu Huibin, stepped forward to stop them and was injured in the head. The thugs then overturned the counter and robbed silver dollars. The store owner took the opportunity to escape and reported to the police station. The police were dispatched to chase and arrest them. The thugs, relying on their numbers, were not afraid. Police officer Zhang Bingjun was also injured. Another policeman snuck back to get reinforcements. All the police officers at the station were dispatched and arrested one of the thugs. The Fengjing branch sent him to Songjiang, who transferred him to the county court for investigation.

Taicang 12

Victim of Economic Oppression A woman surnamed Zhang from Tingziqiao outside the east gate of this city borrowed clothes and jewelry from her neighbors two years ago because her husband was ill. She pawned them at Jitai Pawnshop for twenty silver dollars to pay for her husband's medical expenses. This year, in September, the pawn period expired. On the morning of the 14th, she took advantage of selling chicken feather vegetables. While passing by Jitai Pawnshop, she added six months of interest to the pawned items. After finishing, she continued to sell vegetables at the small vegetable market. At about 9:00 am, she finished selling and went home. When she arrived at the Daoguan Alley, she discovered that all the pawn tickets were lost. She rushed back to the original road to search, but could not find them. Overwhelmed with anxiety, she committed suicide by jumping into the river near the East Gate. By the time people found her, she had already died. How tragic!

Jiangbei Military and Police Suppress Hidden Bandits Chen Diaoyuan, the general commander of the First Route in Jiangbei, believes that scattered bandits are causing trouble everywhere in Jiangbei. This will facilitate the suppression. During the suppression, if police officers and security forces in each county are found wearing plain clothes, carrying rifles or box guns, and not carrying the signs of the security forces, they will be treated as bandits and taken back for questioning.

Zhenjiang 18

Chamber of Commerce Borrows Money to Help Silk Mills According to letters from silk mills such as Hualun, the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce said that recently, due to the sharp drop in silk prices and the impact of artificial silk filling the market, the losses have been considerable. In addition, since the flood, all industries have been depressed, inventory has been piled up, and sales have been sluggish. Although they are trying to resume operations, the silk price continues to fall sharply, and financial turnover is not working. They are bound to stop production. The Department of Industry and Commerce has witnessed the decline of silk and sericulture and is doing its best to maintain and support them. This is because the industry is of great importance to the national economy and people's livelihood. Your Chamber of Commerce is the barrier of commerce and will certainly sympathize with the current difficult situation of our mills and provide appropriate assistance. We would like to request 100,000 yuan of the 1 million yuan of construction bonds borrowed from the provincial government by your chamber last year to maintain the current situation. We will abide by your instructions on how to repay it in the future. The letter was forwarded to the Department of Industry and Commerce. The Department of Industry and Commerce replied that raw silk is China's main export commodity and occupies an important position in exports. Therefore, the prosperity of silk mills not only affects the livelihood of farmers, but also concerns national tax revenue and should be maintained. We have approved the request and requested the Department of Finance to handle it accordingly.

Local News

Xu Mo, Following Luo's Instructions,

Carries Protest Letter and Note Draft

To Shanghai to Consult with Wang and Song

Seeking Final Decision

According to the Central News Agency, the issue of Japan's recognition of the Northeast puppet organization has aroused serious attention worldwide. The Chinese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided to lodge a strong protest with Japan and formally notify the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty of Japan's reckless actions, such as occupying the Northeast territory of China by force and administering it. The notification has already been drafted. Foreign Minister Luo Wengan, because Premier Wang Jingwei is in Shanghai for medical treatment and Acting Premier Song Ziwen is also in Shanghai on official business, specially sent Vice Foreign Minister Xu Mo to Shanghai at 8:05 AM yesterday, carrying the notification to the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty and the protest letter draft, to consult with Wang and Song and make the final decision. The details are recorded as follows:

Consulting with Wang and Song After arriving in Shanghai at 8:05 AM yesterday, Xu rested at the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. At around 10:00 AM, he drove to Premier Wang's former residence on Xipushilu Road to inquire about the final diplomatic decision regarding Japan's recognition of the puppet organization and to express concern for Wang's illness and urge him to return to Beijing as soon as possible. At 11:30 AM, he left with Peng Xuepei, Director of the Political Affairs Department of the Executive Yuan. After Xu left, he went to Qiqilu to visit Acting Premier Song Ziwen. Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, also arrived shortly after and discussed matters with him at Song's residence and had lunch. Xu left at about 1:00 PM and went directly to the North Railway Station, taking special train P.C. 502 and leaving Shanghai for Beijing at 1:30 PM.

Xu's Remarks After Xu left after consulting with Wang, a Central News Agency reporter inquired about the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' policy for responding to Japan's reckless recognition of the puppet organization. According to Xu, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had already decided on the overall policy for responding to Japan's recognition of the Northeast puppet organization and would proceed according to this established policy. Japan was scheduled to recognize the puppet organization this morning (i.e., yesterday), and our government would receive the official report this afternoon (i.e., yesterday). The protest letter to Japan and the notification to the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty would be issued after receiving the official report, and so on.

After the Japanese Acknowledge the Puppet Organization 19

Various circles express different views

Eager to Acknowledge the Reason

Violating the Convention and Disregarding Dignity

Telegraphing to Request the Recall of the Resident Ambassador

Submitting a Petition Requesting a Clear Order to Suppress

Song Ziwen Discusses the Reuters Shanghai News of the 15th: Chinese Minister of Finance Song Ziwen told Reuters reporters today that the Lytton Report has been drafted and will be released in a few weeks. Is this why the Japanese government is so eager to recognize "Manchukuo"? Is this not saying that Japan is deeply afraid that the Lytton Report will determine that the so-called Manchukuo government is purely a puppet created by Japan, and that the so-called representatives of the people of the Three Eastern Provinces are purely castles in the air? Just look at the rising tide of volunteers in the Three Eastern Provinces, whose momentum is growing daily, causing transportation throughout the region to come to a standstill. Moreover, Shenyang, Changchun, and Harbin have been attacked. With the situation like this, to say that the people of the Three Eastern Provinces are eager to create a new nation is simply delirious nonsense. If Japan were to allow an impartial investigation and have nothing to fear, why would it not wait for the results of the investigation to be announced? Japanese soldiers naturally hold a strange theory that if Japan does not recognize the puppet organization it created before the League of Nations meeting considers the Lytton Report, it would inevitably show weakness and lack of determination. However, this kind of theory is only worthy of children whistling in the dark, he said.

Scholars' Opinions According to the Dalu News: Yesterday, the reporter inquired about the opinions of two international law scholars in this port on the Japanese decision to recognize the puppet state. Both stated that the Japanese action is indeed a violation of the Nine-Power Treaty, because the signatory countries to the treaty must respect the territorial and administrative integrity of China. Recently, relevant parties have put forward a new argument, believing that according to the text of the treaty, the signatory countries respect, rather than guarantee, the territorial and administrative integrity of China. According to the opinion of the first expert, respect and guarantee do seem to be different. But, one may ask, how can a country express its respect for the territorial and administrative integrity of another country? It must be by not infringing upon it or causing it any harm. The Japanese claim that the puppet state is the result of national self-determination. Only those who are ignorant of the fact that the puppet state was produced after the Japanese army occupied Manchuria can believe this. In short, regardless of whether there is a difference in the meaning of respect and guarantee, it is not important to Japan, because in any case, Japan has committed the crime of violating the treaty. However, in other countries, these two words have a significant distinction, because if there is an obligation to guarantee, then there is an active obligation to prevent the territorial and administrative integrity of China from being infringed upon. However, Japan's public recognition of the puppet state before the League of Nations meeting is forcing the League of Nations to make a substantial claim. According to the opinion of the second expert, the countries of the Nine-Power Treaty signed with good faith, and should abide by it with good faith. The treaty is not a legal clause, and there are many loopholes. If Japan wants to distort the text to excuse itself, it is easy to do so, because the treaty is a kind of agreement of consent. At the time of signing, it was deeply believed that all countries would be able to faithfully abide by it and be bound by it. Today, the Japanese argument that the treaty is about respect rather than guarantee cannot be called an argument, but can only be regarded as an excuse.

Various Trade Associations Telegraph The various trade associations in this city telegraphed the National Government yesterday, saying (titles omitted): The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in response to the Ambassador Jiang's protest against the recognition of the puppet organization, stated that this is a settled policy and there is no room for change. Today's newspapers reported that the Japanese Privy Council has passed the recognition bill and instructed Mutō to sign a treaty with the puppet state. This has already declared the Three Eastern Provinces to be the second Korea, and China need not ask about it. On the one hand, it is said that China and Japan should maintain friendly relations on a new footing. On the other hand, it is swallowing up the Eastern Provinces and scheming for Chinese interests. This is like strangling someone's throat, causing their death, and yet saying, "I am a good friend to you." This is simply regarding the government and the entire nation as confused and lost. Under these circumstances, the only thing to do is to recall the ambassador stationed in Tokyo, and only give the Japanese ambassador in China courtesy treatment in etiquette, but not engage in official contact, expressing that under these circumstances, there is no way for China and Japan to have any dealings. A little national dignity is retained. At the end of the telegram, the grief and indignation are extreme. Shanghai City North-South Goods Exchange Industry, Silk and Satin Industry, Mineral Ash Industry, Flying Flower Industry, Sugar Industry, Intestine Industry, Rice Shop Industry, Mercerized Cotton Velvet Industry, and other sixty-odd trade associations kowtow, deleted and printed.

The General Union Telegrams The General Labor Union of this city telegraphed the Central Government yesterday, saying: Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, National Government, in your judgment, Japan has already seized the Northeast by force, and has used one hand to create the puppet government of Manchukuo. Our entire nation, in order to maintain sovereignty and preserve territory, vows to never recognize it. All responsibilities should be borne by Japan. Now, the violent Japanese have become even more intensified and unscrupulous, and today they have specially dispatched a plenipotentiary envoy, Mutō, to Changchun to sign an agreement with the puppet state, giving it formal recognition. Its destruction of the Nine-Power Treaty and undermining of international covenants is already obvious. And its hideous and terrifying face has also been completely exposed. This kind of action by Japan has long been expected by us. Our government authorities, at this moment of shattered rivers and mountains, changing territory, precarious national situation, and critical juncture, must decisively order the prompt dispatch of elite troops to launch an expedition, drive out the ugly captives, and restore our rivers and mountains, in order to punish national traitors and protect national rights. At the end of the telegram, blood spurts out, and there is utmost urgency, etc. Shanghai General Labor Union kowtows, deleted.

Military and Political Authorities 21

Preventing the September 18th Incident

Deeply Afraid of Popular Indignation

To Avoid Diplomatic Disputes

Separate Preparations and Precautions

The Garrison Headquarters, according to the Far East News Agency, with the approaching one-week anniversary of the September 18th National Crisis, and with the Japanese formally signing the treaty recognizing the puppet organization at this time of popular indignation, our authorities are deeply afraid that the general public, driven by momentary indignation, will take excessive actions that will affect diplomacy. Therefore, the Garrison Headquarters has officially announced martial law to prevent accidents. Starting from the 14th of this month, ordinary martial law will be implemented. At 7:00 p.m. on the 17th, special martial law will be officially announced. In addition to dispatching more police officers to important street intersections, plainclothes detectives will be sent to patrol various locations. After 12:00 a.m., pedestrians will be prohibited from passing.

The Municipal Government, according to the Far East News Agency, the municipal authorities are deeply afraid that popular sentiment will be激昂 on the September 18th holiday, leading to unexpected incidents. In order to avoid diplomatic disputes, yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau was specifically ordered to inform all factories not to stop work on the 18th to avoid accidents. All commemorative ceremonies should be held in the factories. The Education Bureau was also ordered to instruct all schools to strictly prohibit student parades and demonstrations. On the morning of each day, a memorial service should be held in the school, and students should not be allowed to leave the school arbitrarily to avoid accidents, it is said.

Ministry of Transportation 23

Plans to Rectify Telecommunications

Since Huang Shaoxiong, the acting minister of the Ministry of Communications, took office, he has been supervising the Director of the Telecommunications Department, Zhong E, to earnestly rectify the telecommunications business. Since the technical aspect is of utmost importance to communication, it has been practically reformed. The following is what has been learned about its plans that have been formulated and implemented.

Wired Telecommunications (Lines): The speed of telegraph transmission depends entirely on the smoothness of the lines. Therefore, lines are of great importance to telegraphs. In recent years, due to various reasons, the main and branch lines throughout the country have not been effectively repaired, resulting in decaying telegraph poles, rusted wires, and generally poor condition, which are in danger of collapsing completely. However, repairing the main and branch lines at the same time requires a huge amount of money, which is not easy to raise. Therefore, it has been decided to start by repairing the important main lines, and then extend to the secondary main lines and other branch lines. In 1932, it was decided to purchase 25,000 wooden poles, with 20,000 poles used to repair the main lines and 5,000 poles for repairing the branch lines as needed. (Machinery): The communication machinery currently used in various telegraph offices is mostly of the Western and Morse types. Most of these machines are old and dilapidated, and not very responsive. After investigation, it has been determined to prepare the necessary repaired machinery and dispatch specialized staff to various provincial bureaus to collect and repair them separately, with the aim of completely renovating all the original machinery in the country within two years. At the same time, the Nanjing-Xiaguan-Gulou-Tangshan, Hankou-South Branch, Qingdao-Sifang Cang-kou, Jinan-Inner City Receiving and Dispatching Office, Xuzhou Receiving and Dispatching Office, Beiping-Southwest Branch-North Branch-South Branch-West Branch, Zhenjiang-Danyang-Changzhou-Xiaguan-Gulou, and Jiujiang-Hukou four telegraph lines will be replaced with the Ye Sheng machine to save materials. The Kleinschmidt high-speed motor will be used on the Beijing-Shanghai line. The Western telegraph receiving and transmitting machines will be changed to motor-driven to increase speed and expedite communication. (Batteries): The communication power used by various telegraph offices has always been of two types: dry cells and wet batteries. The annual consumption is very large and is not suitable for high-speed motors. The Shanghai Bureau has been ordered to quickly install storage batteries, and the Nanjing, Tianjin, and Beiping bureaus will also be equipped with storage batteries to implement reforms. (Electrical Materials): The engineering and equipment materials needed by the telegraph offices are mostly purchased from abroad, and the annual expenditure is considerable. To save money, it has been decided to improve the various practical machines manufactured by the original telecommunications machinery manufacturing plant to plug the loopholes. At the same time, the level of the materials that must be purchased should be raised, and the electrical testing laboratory should be asked to test the quality of the materials on-site to ensure that the funds are not wasted.

Telephones (City Telephones): 1. Replacing the Batteries in the Pingjin Telephone Bureau. The storage batteries used by the Beiping Telephone East Bureau and the Tianjin Telephone South Bureau have been used for a long time and their effectiveness has been reduced. It has now been decided to purchase and replace the storage batteries. The equipment for the Ping Bureau has already been installed, and the materials for the Jin Bureau are also in transit. 2. Completing the Automatic Machine Projects in Zhangzhou and Shanghai. After the automatic machine projects in the Zhangzhou and Shanghai bureaus were started, the project in Zhangzhou was suspended for several months due to the flood. The project in Shanghai was delayed due to the destruction of the Zhabei external line project after the Shanghai war. It has now been found that the external line materials for the Shanghai Bureau must be repurchased, and the Zhangzhou Bureau also lacks line materials. It has been negotiated with the original dealer to supplement the materials, with the aim of completing this project in a short time. (Long-Distance Telephones): 1. Regarding the Qingpu Long-Distance Line. The Ministry of Communications previously erected a telephone line through Huangdu to Shanghai due to certain considerations. Now that business between Qingpu and Shanghai is busy, the Qing-Hu section of the long-distance telephone has been opened for public use. The section from Huangdu to Qingpu will be temporarily postponed due to the lack of commercial activity. 2. The Number System for the Jinghu Long-Distance Telegraph. When the Beijing-Shanghai long-distance telephone reports the user's number, the original method was to notify each other on the direct line, which took up the line time and was uneconomical. In order to increase the talk time, a phantom device has been installed on the direct line and a listening device has been added for reporting the number.

Radio (International Radio Station): 1. Ordering Submarine Cables for Remote Connection to the International Station. The original remote connection lines between the International Radio Station and the Central Room used open lines and overhead cables. Due to the losses in the previous Shanghai war, and also due to frequent theft, it has now been decided to use underground armored cables instead. A total of fifty pairs of cables, sixteen miles in length, are required from Shanghai to Zhenru and Liuhang. The Ministry of Communications is already purchasing these materials. 2. Moving the International Branch Station Back to its Original Site. The International Branch Station was originally located at the Maple Forest Bridge in West Shanghai. It was moved to Muir Ming Road this spring because of the incident. However, the location is small and temporary in nature, the equipment is crude, and the operation is difficult. The station has now been ordered to move back to its original site to work. (Domestic Radio Station): 1. Re-equipping the Ningtai Machine. The Nanjing Radio Station's transmitting machinery is of an older model and uses an oil engine, which is very expensive. For the sake of reorganization, personnel have been dispatched to bring the machinery to Beijing for re-equipping. The original site of the transmitting station was rented from private houses. Now, taking advantage of the re-equipping period, the Nanjing Station will be moved to the remaining buildings of the Telephone Bureau to save money.

Japanese Naval Action 24

Japanese Marines Also Tighten Security

According to the Dalu News, yesterday (14th) it was learned that the commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, Sakonji, has ordered the Japanese warships under his command to concentrate in the three ports of Hankou, Nanjing, and Shanghai to prevent accidents after Japan recognizes the puppet state and during China's commemoration of September 18th. This order was decided at a meeting of Japanese naval officers in Shanghai on Tuesday night and telegraphed to the Japanese warships along the Yangtze River yesterday morning for compliance. In addition, the Japanese marines in Shanghai have also tightened security. The Japanese troops stationed in the Japanese factories in West Shanghai have also been increased. However, when the Japanese navy's actions were inquired about at the Japanese embassy, they claimed that they did not know and said that they were deployed by the commander of the Third Fleet and did not involve the embassy or consulates. It was also learned that before the Japanese naval officers' meeting on Tuesday, the Japanese commander had received direct instructions from Tokyo, notifying that the treaty signed between Japan and the puppet state would be signed at 11:00 a.m. this morning in Changchun. At the same time, the declaration of recognition of the puppet state would be sent to various countries, instructing them to take appropriate precautions. As a result, the police of the Japanese consulate here also increased by eighty people yesterday. After arriving in Shanghai from Japan, they were sent to patrol the vicinity of the Japanese embassy and consulate and the areas where Japanese residents live, it is said.

The so-called reform of politics and economy should take the revitalization of industry and the encouragement of production as the premise. When he returned to Shanghai, he did not meet Mr. Sun Zhesheng when he passed through Hong Kong. It is said that he will take a certain French mail ship coming to Shanghai next time, but he does not know for sure. Yesterday 27

The Chinese Authorities in the Concession Strictly Prevented Communists

No Incidents Occurred in the Evening, Passing Peacefully

The Chinese authorities in this city's concession received a report yesterday that the Communists would hold an anti-imperialist conference on the 15th, and took temporary precautions. The details are as follows.

Temporary Precautions The Public Security Bureau's district police stations were ordered to double-guard all key roads. Inspectors, detectives, and female inspectors were all on duty, inspecting pedestrians at Ximen and Xiaodongmen. The French Concession's various police stations were ordered to be on alert, with the strictest measures at the intersection of the French Concession and the Chinese area, the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Avenue Foch, and the intersection of the British and French Concessions. The Public Concession's various police stations issued orders to be heavily guarded in Yinxiang Port, Hudong, and Huxi. Chinese and Western detectives went out to patrol.

Preventing Assemblies Yesterday, the Communists heard that the Public Concession and the French Concession police agencies, which were originally scheduled to gather at the intersection of South Chengdu Road, the intersection of Avenue Edward VII, and in front of the Guanghua Grand Theater at 1:30 p.m. to hold a conference, dispatched armed Chinese and Western detectives to rush to the scene to deploy defenses in advance. The inspection of pedestrians in the vicinity was very strict. Although people resembling workers and students were found lingering nearby, they could not gather due to the tight security and dispersed one after another. By 5:00 p.m., the stationed detectives began to withdraw. Everything was normal in the evening, and no incidents occurred.

Recent News on the Baoshan Seawall Project 31

Since the start of the Baoshan Seawall project in late June, the work has been extremely diligent, so its progress has been very rapid. All the progress has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the post-disaster reconstruction project, the military follow-up engineering project, and the emergency rescue project have all been completed by the deadline of September 10. Currently, various registration forms are being processed and submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction and the Jiangnan Seawall Post-Disaster Committee for joint inspection and acceptance, in order to conclude the project.

The main text of the judgment is: the original judgment is revoked; You Bolu is sentenced to four years of imprisonment for the crime of joint homicide; The remaining five policemen Liu Weicheng, He Zhanyou, Wu Maolin, Qiao Xuechang, and Lin Qingxiang are each sentenced to three years and four months of imprisonment. Scheduled to Open on September 18th

Shanghai's famous national goods factories, China Chemical Industry Co., Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, Wuhe Silk Weaving Factory, China First Knitting Factory, Sanyou Industrial Society, Shengde Weaving Factory, Huafu Hat Factory, Yixin Toothbrush Factory, China Enamel Factory, and other nine factories, in order to promote national goods and commemorate the September 18th Incident, have jointly established a nine-factory national goods temporary market opposite the Hong Temple on Nanjing Road. Shantou National Goods Group 39

Representative Cai Xuetian Returned to Guangdong Yesterday

He Spoke About the Decline of National Products and Relief Measures Before Leaving

Cai Xuetian, representative of the Guangdong Shantou China National Goods Maintenance Association, who came north to investigate the situation of national products in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, began to investigate the situation of national products in Shanghai after returning to Shanghai from Hangzhou. The investigation work has largely been completed. Yesterday, Cai took a boat back to Guangdong. Before leaving, he spoke about the reasons for the decline of national products and relief measures. His words were quite pertinent and are specially recorded. He said, "The decline of national products is painful to talk about. However, to summarize the reasons, they can be divided into several points: (1) Most Chinese people cannot practically use national goods, and they treat the promotion of national goods as a fashionable slogan. Therefore, those who advocate national goods in words but still wear foreign goods are everywhere. (2) The government's protection and encouragement of national products is just a piece of empty paper and does not help in practice. (3) There is a lack of talent and insufficient capital, which fails to create a substantial and effective struggle against foreign goods. (4) National products do not have significant progress. Due to environmental factors, the treatment of workers has not been able to satisfy them, resulting in frequent labor unrest and self-destructive opportunities." Due to the above points, national products have no development at all, and the country has become a market for international capitalists. The amount of leakage is incalculable. However, the past is gone, and the future can be pursued. Today, Chinese people should learn from the past and strive to find relief measures. Otherwise, if this continues, the national economy will inevitably lead to total bankruptcy. In my opinion, in the future, (1) domestic media, with their foresight and wisdom, should sincerely and jointly promote national products with enthusiastic people to promote the awakening of Chinese people and unanimously use domestic products. (2) Prevent the destruction of evil forces and give national products a chance to revive. (3) Find ways to reduce the burden on national goods and strengthen the power to fight foreign goods. (4) Train talents for manufacturing national goods, increase the capital for developing national products, and improve the quality of goods. (5) Give preferential treatment to workers to stabilize their lives and achieve effective cooperation. If we can do this, why worry about the lack of prosperity of national products and the lack of foreign goods? In short, now that the country is in trouble, I believe that all living beings can make up their minds to go to the national crisis. However, using active methods to seek the revival of national products (1) can consolidate the national economy (2) can prevent the economic imperialists from coveting our land. This is also a way to save the country," he said.

All Workers of Sanyou Factory 43

Went to the Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday to Petition

The Employer Refused to Pay for Meals

Party and Government Discussing Effective Measures

According to Dagongshe, the dispute over the closure of the Sanyou Industrial Society in Yinxiang Township, Pudong, has already been legally ruled by the municipal government. However, the employer declared an objection and refused to pay for meals for the second consecutive time, causing panic among all the workers. Yesterday morning, all the workers went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, the situation as follows:

Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, representatives Hong Jiaben and Liu Yushan, delegated by the starving workers of the factory, went to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, stating the suffering of the workers and requesting the party and government organs to take effective measures. Then, at about 9:00 AM, more than 600 workers gathered again, wearing symbols, and went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, and elected Zuo Zhongzhao, Bao Boyi, Zhang Tingliang, Lian Xinzhi, Wu Renfu, and Qin Haiyan as representatives, who were received by Wang Xianqing. The representatives first stated the purpose of the petition, and the bureau representative expressed acceptance. However, during this period of martial law, the large number of people was an obstacle to local security. The workers were asked to withdraw first and return to the factory, otherwise they would not be able to go to the municipal government together. The workers insisted on not agreeing. Later, Xu Yefu, director of the Third Section, explained in detail to the workers, and his words were earnest, saying that if the employer insisted on not paying, the Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau would seek practical solutions. The workers felt satisfied and returned to the factory in formation.

Representatives Zhong Quan from the Municipal Party Department, Wang Xianqing from the Social Affairs Bureau, and Dong Shihe from the Public Security Bureau, together with Zhang Linhua and Lu Lianqing, directors of the Fifth District Shipbuilding Labor Union, went to the Sanyou Society to negotiate. Because the person in charge of the company avoided meeting, Mei Xiji, an important staff member, was received. According to him, the board of directors had already decided not to pay for the workers' meals. The representatives immediately went to the municipal government to report everything, and Secretary-General Yu and the party and government representatives discussed effective methods, limiting the employer to send the two meal fees to the Social Affairs Bureau this morning, and instructing the labor representatives to receive them at the bureau.

Labor Dispute in the Candle Industry 44

Opposing the Employer's Use of Non-Members

Party and Government Organs Conducting Mediation

All the employees in the candle industry in this city have been provoked by the fact that the sellers violated the Labor Record No. 57 signed by the Labor Mediation Committee on February 2, 1920, resulting in a labor dispute. It is reported that the party and government organs are prepared to conduct mediation. The text of the application submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau by Chen Zenghao and other representatives of the candle industry union is recorded below: It is hereby submitted that the employer does not abide by the contract and uses non-members to work. Repeated negotiations have been ineffective. It is requested to convene both parties to mediate. Before the association was reorganized, it was ordered to be disbanded. Now, it is applying for reorganization according to law. Unexpectedly, the employer did not abide by the contract and used non-members to work when the association was not strong. Repeated negotiations have yielded no results. It should be noted that our labor-capital contract was signed with the industry association in 1920 with amendments by your bureau. Article 4 of the contract stated that the store should only hire members of the union. Now, the employer is using non-members to work, which is obviously breaking the contract and causing disputes. The general members of the association are indignant because the members of the first industry were affected by the Shanghai war. It was requested to convene representatives of various workshops to discuss. The association convened a meeting of representatives on the 11th. It was generally agreed that the current unemployment problem is still unresolved, and the scope of work has been invaded by others. Our workers are forced by life. No matter what sacrifices there may be, they are determined to fight the employer to the death. The association, seeing the serious situation, immediately dissuaded the members from taking any unruly actions and increasing disputes. At the same time, it sent a letter to your bureau, sincerely requesting a speedy convening of mediation so as to obtain a peaceful solution and avoid the expansion of the storm and affecting local security. This is a public convenience.

Hong Kong National Ship Resumes Sailing 47

Stopped Sailing for Five or Six Years

Resuming Within This Month

Hong Kong Customs' inspection of Chinese ships is the most stringent. Ships that are older or slightly non-compliant will not be given a ship's license and will not be able to sail in Hong Kong. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hong Kong liners have been jointly operated by Nanhua ships. Originally, there were two ships, Xinhua and Xinchang. After the two ships were wrecked and sunk, none of the company's ships met the regulations for sailing to Hong Kong, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company effectively abandoned the navigation rights to the port of Hong Kong, which has been going on for four or five years.

Negotiations between the Hong Kong Bureau and Shanghai Chinese Ships Although most Chinese ships other than those of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company only sail to Shantou, Xiamen, and Guangzhou, none go to Hong Kong. Not only have the navigation rights been lost and the shipping business between Shanghai and Hong Kong has been taken by British and Japanese foreign ships, but it also indicates that no Chinese seagoing ship can go to Hong Kong, which is truly shameful. The China Merchants Port Bureau negotiated with Hong Kong Customs and prepared to resume service. After more than a month, it has been successful. Hong Kong Customs has approved the issuance of ship's licenses.

Fair Inaugural Service The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Nanhai liners Hairui and Haixiang have been abandoned on the Longhua River. The Fair is the largest of the company's ships. In order to restore the Hong Kong route, the Fair was sent to the factory for repairs and the passenger seats were rebuilt to comply with Hong Kong Customs regulations. It will soon be completed and is scheduled to start the regular Hong Kong service after the 20th of this month.
